1.24.0</option><option value="1.23.0">Version 1.23.0</option><option value="1.22.0">Version 1.22.0</option></select></label></form></div><div class="code-desc"><p>A simulated Streamlit app to check the correctness of displayed    elements and outputs.</p>
<p>An instance of <tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> simulates a running Streamlit app. This class
provides methods to set up, manipulate, and inspect the app contents via
API instead of a browser UI. It can be used to write automated tests of an
app in various scenarios. These can then be run using a tool like pytest.</p>
<p><tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> can be initialized by one of three class methods:</p>
<ul class="simple">
<li><a class="reference external" href="#apptestfrom_file"><tt class="docutils literal">st.testing.v1.AppTest.from_file</tt></a> (recommended)</li>
<li><a class="reference external" href="#apptestfrom_string"><tt class="docutils literal">st.testing.v1.AppTest.from_string</tt></a></li>
<li><a class="reference external" href="#apptestfrom_function"><tt class="docutils literal">st.testing.v1.AppTest.from_function</tt></a></li>
</ul>
<p>Once initialized, Session State and widget values can be updated and the
script can be run. Unlike an actual live-running Streamlit app, you need to
call <tt class="docutils literal">AppTest.run()</tt> explicitly to re-run the app after changing a widget
value. Switching pages also requires an explicit, follow-up call to
<tt class="docutils literal">AppTest.run()</tt>.</p>
<p><tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> enables developers to build tests on their app as-is, in the
familiar python test format, without major refactoring or abstracting out
logic to be tested separately from the UI. Tests can run quickly with very
low overhead. A typical pattern is to build a suite of tests for an app
that ensure consistent functionality as the app evolves, and run the tests
locally and/or in a CI environment like Github Actions.</p>
<div class="admonition note">
<p class="first admonition-title">Note</p>
<p class="last"><tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> only supports testing a single page of an app per
instance. For multipage apps, each page will need to be tested
separately. <tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> is not yet compatible with multipage apps
using <tt class="docutils literal">st.navigation</tt> and <tt class="docutils literal">st.Page</tt>.</p>
</div>

value="1.23.0">Version 1.23.0</option><option value="1.22.0">Version 1.22.0</option></select></label></form></div><div class="code-desc"><p>Create an instance of <tt class="docutils literal">AppTest</tt> to simulate an app page defined        within a file.</p>
<p>This option is most convenient for CI workflows and testing of
published apps. The script must be executable on its own and so must
contain all necessary imports.</p>
</div></div><section class="table_TableContainer__JWglo"><table class="full-width table_Table__xjBId"><thead><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM table_HeadingRow__zGCcZ"><th class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_TitleCell__m1zdo" colSpan="2">Function signature<a href="https://github.com/streamlit/streamlit/blob/1.52.0/lib/streamlit/testing/v1/app_test.py#L276" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" title="View st.from_file source code on GitHub">[source]</a></th></tr><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM"><th class="table_Cell__NwRF3" colSpan="2"><p class='code'> AppTest.from_file(cls, script_path, *, default_timeout=3)</p> </th></tr></thead><tbody><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM table_HeadingRow__zGCcZ"><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_TitleCell__m1zdo" colSpan="2">Parameters</td></tr><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM"><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_SmallCell__b_IbF"><div>
        <p class="
          
          
        ">
          <span class='bold'>script_path</span>
          <span class='italic code'>(str | Path)</span>
        </p>
      </div> </td><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_BigCell__wOqnZ"><div>
        
        <p>Path to a script file. The path should be absolute or relative to
the file calling <tt class="docutils literal">.from_file</tt>.</p>

      </div></td></tr><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM"><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_SmallCell__b_IbF"><div>
        <p class="
          
          autofunction_Keyword__c8FQ_
        ">
          <span class='bold'>default_timeout</span>
          <span class='italic code'>(float)</span>
        </p>
      </div> </td><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_BigCell__wOqnZ"><div>
        
        <p>Default time in seconds before a script run is timed out. Can be
overridden for individual <tt class="docutils literal">.run()</tt> calls.</p>

      </div></td></tr></tbody><tfoot><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM table_HeadingRow__zGCcZ"><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_TitleCell__m1zdo" colSpan="2">Returns</td></tr><tr class="table_Row__tz8tM"><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_SmallCell__b_IbF"><div><p><span class='italic code'>(AppTest)</span></p> </div> </td><td class="table_Cell__NwRF3 table_BigCell__wOqnZ"><div><p>A simulated Streamlit app for testing. The simulated app can be
executed via <tt class="docutils literal">.run()</tt>.</p>

occurs upon user interaction. <tt class="docutils literal">AppTest.run()</tt> must be manually called

7.50952C7.25103 7.50952 7.3049 7.50952 7.34082 7.47388Z" fill="#808495"></path></svg></div></h1>
<p>The main value of <code>AppTest</code> is providing an API to programmatically inspect and interact with the elements and widgets produced by a running Streamlit app. Using the <code>AppTest.&lt;element type&gt;</code> properties or <code>AppTest.get()</code> method returns a collection of all the elements or widgets of the specified type that would have been displayed by running the app.</p>
<p>Note that you can also retrieve elements within a specific container in the same way - first retrieve the container, then retrieve the elements just in that container.</p>

<p>Each tab within a single <tt class="docutils literal">st.tabs</tt> will be returned as a separate Tab
in the Sequence. Additionally, the tab labels are forwarded to each
Tab element as a property. For example, <tt class="docutils literal"><span class="pre">st.tabs(&quot;A&quot;,&quot;B&quot;)</span></tt> will
yield two Tab objects, with <tt class="docutils literal">Tab.label</tt> returning &quot;A&quot; and &quot;B&quot;,
respectively.</p>
